Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /testbed/compiler-core/src/inline.rs:
     1	//! This module implements the function inlining optimisation. This allows
     2	//! function calls to be inlined at the callsite, and replaced with the contents
     3	//! of the function which is being called.
     4	//!
     5	//! Function inlining is useful for two main reasons:
     6	//! - It removes the overhead of calling other functions and jumping around
     7	//!   execution too much
     8	//! - It removes the barrier of the function call between the code around the
     9	//!   call, and the code inside the called function.
    10	//!
    11	//! For example, the following Gleam code make heavy use of `use` sugar and higher
    12	//! order functions:
    13	//!
    14	//! ```gleam
    15	//! pub fn try_sum(list: List(Result(String, Nil)), sum: Int) -> Result(Int, Nil) {
    16	//!   use <- bool.guard(when: sum >= 1000, return: Ok(sum))
    17	//!   case list {
    18	//!     [] -> Ok(sum)
    19	//!     [first, ..rest] -> {
    20	//!       use number <- result.try(int.parse(first))
    21	//!       try_sum(rest, sum + number)
    22	//!     }
    23	//!   }
    24	//! }
    25	//! ```
    26	//!
    27	//! This can make the code easier to read, but it normally would have a performance
    28	//! cost. There are two called functions, and two implicit anonymous functions.
    29	//! This function is also not tail recursive, as it uses higher order functions
    30	//! inside its body.
    31	//!
    32	//! However, with function inlining, the above code can be optimised to:
    33	//!
    34	//! ```gleam
    35	//! pub fn try_sum(list: List(Result(String, Nil)), sum: Int) -> Result(Int, Nil) {
    36	//!   case sum >= 1000 {
    37	//!     True -> Ok(sum)
    38	//!     False -> case list {
    39	//!       [] -> Ok(sum)
    40	//!       [first, ..rest] -> {
    41	//!         case int.parse(first) {
    42	//!           Ok(number) -> try_sum(rest, sum + number)
    43	//!           Error(error) -> Error(error)
    44	//!         }
    45	//!       }
    46	//!     }
    47	//!   }
    48	//! }
    49	//! ```
    50	//!
    51	//! Which now has no extra function calls, and is tail recursive!
    52	//!
    53	//! The process of function inlining is quite simple really. It is implemented
    54	//! using an AST folder, which traverses each node of the AST, and potentially
    55	//! alters it as it goes.
    56	//!
    57	//! Every time we encounter a function call, we decide whether or not we can
    58	//! inline it. For now, the criteria for inlining is very simple, although a
    59	//! more complex heuristic-based approach will likely be implemented in the
    60	//! future. For now though, a function can be inlined if:
    61	//! It is a standard library function within the hardcoded list - which can be
    62	//! found in the `inline_function` function - or, it is an anonymous function.
    63	//!
    64	//! Inlining anonymous functions allows us to:
    65	//! - Remove calls to parameters of higher-order functions once those higher-
    66	//!   order functions have been inlined. For example, the following example using
    67	//!   `result.map`:
    68	//!   ```gleam
    69	//!   result.map(Ok(10), fn(x) { x + 1 })
    70	//!   ```
    71	//!
    72	//!   Without inlining of anonymous function would be turned into:
    73	//!   ```gleam
    74	//!   case Ok(10) {
    75	//!     Ok(value) -> Ok(fn(x) { x + 1 }(value))
    76	//!     Error(error) -> Error(error)
    77	//!   }
    78	//!   ```
    79	//!
    80	//!   However if we inline anonymous functions also, we remove every call, and
    81	//!   so it becomes:
    82	//!
    83	//!   ```gleam
    84	//!   case Ok(10) {
    85	//!     Ok(value) -> Ok(value + 1)
    86	//!     Error(error) -> Error(error)
    87	//!   }
    88	//!   ```
    89	//!
    90	//! - Remove calls to anonymous functions in pipelines. Sometimes, an anonymous
    91	//!   function is used in a pipeline, which can sometimes be the result of an
    92	//!   expanded function capture. For example:
    93	//!
    94	//!   ```gleam
    95	//!   "10" |> int.parse |> result.unwrap(0) |> fn(x) { x * x } |> something_else
    96	//!   ```
    97	//!
    98	//!   This can now be desugared to:
    99	//!   ```gleam
   100	//!   let _pipe1 = "10"
   101	//!   let _pipe2 = int.parse(_pipe1)
   102	//!   let _pipe3 = result.unwrap(_pipe2, 0)
   103	//!   let _pipe4 = _pipe3 * _pipe3
   104	//!   something_else(_pipe4)
   105	//!   ```
   106	//!
   107	//! See documentation of individual functions to explain better how the process
   108	//! works.
   109	//!
   110

   137	/// Perform function inlining across an entire module, applying it to each
   138	/// individual function.
   139	pub fn module(
   140	    mut module: TypedModule,
   141	    modules: &im::HashMap<EcoString, ModuleInterface>,
   142	) -> TypedModule {
   143	    let mut inliner = Inliner::new(modules);
   144	
   145	    module.definitions = module
   146	        .definitions
   147	        .into_iter()
   148	        .map(|definition| inliner.definition(definition))
   149	        .collect();
   150	    module
   151	}
   152	
   153	struct Inliner<'a> {
   154	    /// Importable modules, containing information about functions which can be
   155	    /// inlined
   156	    modules: &'a im::HashMap<EcoString, ModuleInterface>,
   157	    /// Any variables which can be inlined. This is used when inlining the body
   158	    /// of function calls. Let's look at an example inlinable function:
   159	    /// ```gleam
   160	    /// pub fn add(a, b) {
   161	    ///   a + b
   162	    /// }
   163	    /// ```
   164	    /// If it is called - `add(1, 2)` - it can be inlined to the following:
   165	    /// ```gleam
   166	    /// {
   167	    ///   let a = 1
   168	    ///   let b = 2
   169	    ///   a + b
   170	    /// }
   171	    /// ```
   172	    ///
   173	    /// However, this can be inlined further. Since `a` and `b` are only used
   174	    /// once each in the body, the whole expression can be reduced to `1 + 2`.
   175	    ///
   176	    /// In the above example, this variable would contain `{a: 1, b: 2}`,
   177	    /// indicating the names of the variables to be inlined, as well as the
   178	    /// values to replace them with.
   179	    inline_variables: HashMap<EcoString, TypedExpr>,
   180	}
   181	
   182	impl Inliner<'_> {
   183	    fn new(modules: &im::HashMap<EcoString, ModuleInterface>) -> Inliner<'_> {
   184	        Inliner {
   185	            modules,
   186	            inline_variables: HashMap::new(),
   187	        }
   188	    }
   189	
   190	    /// Perform inlining over a single definition. This only does anything for
   191	    /// function definitions as none of the other definitions can contain call
   192	    /// expressions to be inlined.
   193	    fn definition(&mut self, definition: TypedDefinition) -> TypedDefinition {
   194	        match definition {
   195	            Definition::Function(function_ast) => Definition::Function(self.function(function_ast)),
   196	            Definition::TypeAlias(_)
   197	            | Definition::CustomType(_)
   198	            | Definition::Import(_)
   199	            | Definition::ModuleConstant(_) => definition,
   200	        }
   201	    }
   202	
   203	    fn function(&mut self, mut function: TypedFunction) -> TypedFunction {
   204	        function.body = function.body.mapped(|statement| self.statement(statement));
   205	        function
   206	    }
   207	
   208	    fn statement(&mut self, statement: TypedStatement) -> TypedStatement {
   209	        match statement {
   210	            Statement::Expression(expression_ast) => {
   211	                Statement::Expression(self.expression(expression_ast))
   212	            }
   213	            Statement::Assignment(assignment_ast) => {
   214	                Statement::Assignment(Box::new(self.assignment(*assignment_ast)))
   215	            }
   216	            Statement::Use(use_ast) => Statement::Use(self.use_(use_ast)),
   217	            Statement::Assert(assert_ast) => Statement::Assert(self.assert(assert_ast)),
   218	        }
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    fn assert(&mut self, assert: TypedAssert) -> TypedAssert {
   222	        let Assert {
   223	            location,
   224	            value,
   225	            message,
   226	        } = assert;
   227	
   228	        Assert {
   229	            location,
   230	            value: self.expression(value),
   231	            message: message.map(|expression| self.expression(expression)),
   232	        }
   233	    }
   234	
   235	    fn use_(&mut self, mut use_: TypedUse) -> TypedUse {
   236	        use_.call = self.boxed_expression(use_.call);
   237	        use_
   238	    }
   239	
   240	    fn assignment(&mut self, assignment: TypedAssignment) -> TypedAssignment {
   241	        let Assignment {
   242	            location,
   243	            value,
   244	            pattern,
   245	            kind,
   246	            annotation,
   247	            compiled_case,
   248	        } = assignment;
   249	
   250	        Assignment {
   251	            location,
   252	            value: self.expression(value),
   253	            pattern,
   254	            kind: self.assignment_kind(kind),
   255	            annotation,
   256	            compiled_case,
   257	        }
   258	    }
   259	
   260	    fn assignment_kind(&mut self, kind: AssignmentKind<TypedExpr>) -> AssignmentKind<TypedExpr> {
   261	        match kind {
   262	            AssignmentKind::Let | AssignmentKind::Generated => kind,
   263	            AssignmentKind::Assert {
   264	                location,
   265	                assert_keyword_start,
   266	                message,
   267	            } => AssignmentKind::Assert {
   268	                location,
   269	                assert_keyword_start,
   270	                message: message.map(|expression| self.expression(expression)),
   271	            },
   272	        }
   273	    }
   274	
   275	    fn boxed_expression(&mut self, boxed: Box<TypedExpr>) -> Box<TypedExpr> {
   276	        Box::new(self.expression(*boxed))
   277	    }
   278	
   279	    fn expressions(&mut self, expressions: Vec<TypedExpr>) -> Vec<TypedExpr> {
   280	        expressions
   281	            .into_iter()
   282	            .map(|expression| self.expression(expression))
   283	            .collect()
   284	    }
   285	
   286	    /// Perform inlining over an expression. This function is recursive, as
   287	    /// expressions can be deeply nested. Most expressions just recursively
   288	    /// call this function on each of their component parts, but some have
   289	    /// special handling.
   290	    fn expression(&mut self, expression: TypedExpr) -> TypedExpr {
   291	        match expression {
   292	            TypedExpr::Int { .. }
   293	            | TypedExpr::Float { .. }
   294	            | TypedExpr::String { .. }
   295	            | TypedExpr::Fn { .. }
   296	            | TypedExpr::ModuleSelect { .. }
   297	            | TypedExpr::Invalid { .. } => expression,
   298	
   299	            TypedExpr::Var {
   300	                ref constructor,
   301	                ref name,
   302	                ..
   303	            } => match &constructor.variant {
   304	                // If this variable can be inlined, replace it with its value.
   305	                // See the `inline_variables` documentation for an explanation.
   306	                ValueConstructorVariant::LocalVariable { .. } => {
   307	                    // We remove the variable as inlined variables can only be
   308	                    // inlined once. `inline_variables` only contains variables
   309	                    // which we have already checked are possible to inline, as
   310	                    // we check for variables which are only used once when converting
   311	                    // to an `InlinableFunction`.
   312	                    match self.inline_variables.remove(name) {
   313	                        Some(inlined_expression) => inlined_expression,
   314	                        None => expression,
   315	                    }
   316	                }
   317	                ValueConstructorVariant::ModuleConstant { .. }
   318	                | ValueConstructorVariant::LocalConstant { .. }
   319	                | ValueConstructorVariant::ModuleFn { .. }
   320	                | ValueConstructorVariant::Record { .. } => expression,
   321	            },
   322	
   323	            TypedExpr::Block {
   324	                location,
   325	                statements,
   326	            } => TypedExpr::Block {
   327	                location,

   329	            },
   330	
   331	            TypedExpr::NegateBool { location, value } => TypedExpr::NegateBool {
   332	                location,
   333	                value: self.boxed_expression(value),
   334	            },
   335	
   336	            TypedExpr::NegateInt { location, value } => TypedExpr::NegateInt {

   348	
   349	            TypedExpr::List {

   359	            },
   360	
   361	            TypedExpr::Call {
   362	                location,
   363	                type_,
   364	                fun,
   365	                arguments,
   366	            } => self.call(location, type_, fun, arguments),
   367	
   368	            TypedExpr::BinOp {
   369	                location,
   370	                type_,
   371	                name,
   372	                name_location,

   557	    fn call(
   558	        &mut self,
   559	        location: SrcSpan,
   560	        type_: Arc<Type>,
   561	        function: Box<TypedExpr>,
   562	        arguments: Vec<TypedCallArg>,
   563	    ) -> TypedExpr {
   564	        let arguments = arguments
   565	            .into_iter()
   566	            .map(
   567	                |TypedCallArg {
   568	                     label,
   569	                     location,
   570	                     value,
   571	                     implicit,
   572	                 }| TypedCallArg {
   573	                    label,
   574	                    location,
   575	                    value: self.expression(value),
   576	                    implicit,
   577	                },
   578	            )
   579	            .collect();
   580	
   581	        // First, we traverse the left-hand side of this call. If this is called
   582	        // inside another inlined function, this could potentially inline an
   583	        // argument, allowing further inlining.
   584	        let function = self.expression(*function);
   585	
   586	        // If the left-hand side is in a block for some reason, for example
   587	        // `{ fn(x) { x + 1 } }(10)`, we still want to be able to inline it.
   588	        let function = expand_block(function);
   589	
   590	        let function = match function {
   591	            TypedExpr::Var {
   592	                ref constructor,
   593	                ref name,
   594	                ..
   595	            } => match &constructor.variant {
   596	                ValueConstructorVariant::ModuleFn { module, .. } => {
   597	                    // If the function is in the list of inlinable functions in
   598	                    // the module it belongs to, we can inline it!
   599	                    if let Some(function) = self
   600	                        .modules
   601	                        .get(module)
   602	                        .and_then(|module| module.inline_functions.get(name))
   603	                    {
   604	                        // First, we do the actual inlining, by converting it to
   605	                        // an anonymous function.
   606	                        let (parameters, body) = function.to_anonymous_function();
   607	                        // Then, we perform beta reduction, inlining the call to
   608	                        // the anonymous function.
   609	                        return self.inline_anonymous_function_call(
   610	                            &parameters,
   611	                            arguments,
   612	                            body,
   613	                            &function.inlinable_parameters,
   614	                        );
   615	                    } else {
   616	                        function
   617	                    }
   618	                }
   619	                // We cannot inline local variables or constants, as we do not
   620	                // have enough information to inline them. Records are not actually
   621	                // function calls, so they also cannot be inlined.
   622	                ValueConstructorVariant::LocalVariable { .. }
   623	                | ValueConstructorVariant::ModuleConstant { .. }
   624	                | ValueConstructorVariant::LocalConstant { .. }
   625	                | ValueConstructorVariant::Record { .. } => function,
   626	            },
   627	            TypedExpr::ModuleSelect {
   628	                ref constructor,
   629	                label: ref name,
   630	                ref module_name,
   631	                ..
   632	            } => match constructor {
   633	                // We use the same logic here as for `TypedExpr::Var` above.
   634	                ModuleValueConstructor::Fn { .. } => {
   635	                    if let Some(function) = self
   636	                        .modules
   637	                        .get(module_name)
   638	                        .and_then(|module| module.inline_functions.get(name))
   639	                    {
   640	                        let (parameters, body) = function.to_anonymous_function();
   641	                        return self.inline_anonymous_function_call(
   642	                            &parameters,
   643	                            arguments,
   644	                            body,
   645	                            &function.inlinable_parameters,
   646	                        );
   647	                    } else {
   648	                        function
   649	                    }
   650	                }
   651	                ModuleValueConstructor::Record { .. } | ModuleValueConstructor::Constant { .. } => {
   652	                    function
   653	                }
   654	            },
   655	            // Direct calls to anonymous functions can always be inlined
   656	            TypedExpr::Fn {
   657	                arguments: parameters,
   658	                body,
   659	                ..
   660	            } => {
   661	                let inlinable_parameters = find_inlinable_parameters(&parameters, &body);
   662	                return self.inline_anonymous_function_call(
   663	                    &parameters,
   664	                    arguments,
   665	                    body,
   666	                    &inlinable_parameters,
   667	                );
   668	            }
   669	            TypedExpr::Int { .. }
   670	            | TypedExpr::Float { .. }
   671	            | TypedExpr::String { .. }
   672	            | TypedExpr::Block { .. }
   673	            | TypedExpr::Pipeline { .. }
   674	            | TypedExpr::List { .. }
   675	            | TypedExpr::Call { .. }
   676	            | TypedExpr::BinOp { .. }
   677	            | TypedExpr::Case { .. }
   678	            | TypedExpr::RecordAccess { .. }
   679	            | TypedExpr::Tuple { .. }
   680	            | TypedExpr::TupleIndex { .. }
   681	            | TypedExpr::Todo { .. }
   682	            | TypedExpr::Panic { .. }
   683	            | TypedExpr::Echo { .. }
   684	            | TypedExpr::BitArray { .. }
   685	            | TypedExpr::RecordUpdate { .. }
   686	            | TypedExpr::NegateBool { .. }
   687	            | TypedExpr::NegateInt { .. }
   688	            | TypedExpr::Invalid { .. } => function,
   689	        };
   690	
   691	        TypedExpr::Call {
   692	            location,
   693	            type_,
   694	            fun: Box::new(function),
   695	            arguments,
   696	        }
   697	    }

   700	    fn inline_anonymous_function_call(
   701	        &mut self,
   702	        parameters: &[TypedArg],
   703	        arguments: Vec<TypedCallArg>,
   704	        body: Vec1<TypedStatement>,
   705	        inlinable_parameters: &[EcoString],
   706	    ) -> TypedExpr {
   707	        // Arguments to this call that can be inlined, and do not need an assignment.
   708	        let mut inline = HashMap::new();
   709	
   710	        // We start by collecting all the assignments for parameters which cannot
   711	        // be inlined.
   712	        let mut statements = parameters
   713	            .iter()
   714	            .zip(arguments)
   715	            .filter_map(|(parameter, argument)| {
   716	                let name = parameter.get_variable_name().cloned().unwrap_or("_".into());
   717	
   718	                // An argument can be inlined if it is only used once (stored in
   719	                // the `InlineFunction` structure), and it is pure. Sometime impure
   720	                // arguments can be inlined, but for simplicity we avoid inlining
   721	                // all impure arguments for now. This heuristic can be improved
   722	                // later.
   723	                if inlinable_parameters.contains(&name)
   724	                    && argument.value.is_pure_value_constructor()
   725	                {
   726	                    _ = inline.insert(name, argument.value);
   727	                    return None;
   728	                }
   729	
   730	                let type_ = argument.value.type_();
   731	
   732	                // Otherwise, we make an assignment which assigns the value of
   733	                // the argument to the correct parameter name.
   734	                Some(Statement::Assignment(Box::new(Assignment {
   735	                    location: BLANK_LOCATION,
   736	                    value: argument.value,
   737	                    pattern: TypedPattern::Variable {
   738	                        location: BLANK_LOCATION,
   739	                        name: name.clone(),
   740	                        type_: type_.clone(),
   741	                        origin: VariableOrigin::generated(),
   742	                    },
   743	                    kind: AssignmentKind::Generated,
   744	                    compiled_case: CompiledCase::simple_variable_assignment(name, type_),
   745	                    annotation: None,
   746	                })))
   747	            })
   748	            .collect_vec();
   749	
   750	        // If we are performing inlining within an already inlined function, there
   751	        // might be inlinable variables in the outer scope. However, these cannot be
   752	        // inlined inside a nested function, so they are saved and restored afterwards.
   753	        let inline_variables = std::mem::replace(&mut self.inline_variables, inline);
   754	
   755	        // Perform inlining on each of the statements in this function's body,
   756	        // potentially inlining parameters and function calls inside this function.
   757	        statements.extend(body.into_iter().map(|statement| self.statement(statement)));
   758	
   759	        self.inline_variables = inline_variables;
   760	
   761	        // We try to expand this block, so a function which is inlined as a
   762	        // single expression does not get wrapped unnecessarily
   763	        expand_block(TypedExpr::Block {
   764	            location: BLANK_LOCATION,
   765	            statements: statements
   766	                .try_into()
   767	                .expect("Type checking ensures there is at least one statement"),
   768	        })
   769	    }
   770	
   771	    fn pipeline(
   772	        &mut self,
   773	        location: SrcSpan,
   774	        first_value: TypedPipelineAssignment,
   775	        assignments: Vec<(TypedPipelineAssignment, PipelineAssignmentKind)>,
   776	        finally: Box<TypedExpr>,
   777	        finally_kind: PipelineAssignmentKind,
   778	    ) -> TypedExpr {
   779	        let first_value = self.pipeline_assignment(first_value);
   780	        let assignments = assignments
   781	            .into_iter()
   782	            .map(|(assignment, kind)| (self.pipeline_assignment(assignment), kind))
   783	            .collect();
   784	        let finally = self.boxed_expression(finally);
   785	
   786	        TypedExpr::Pipeline {
   787	            location,
   788	            first_value,
   789	            assignments,
   790	            finally,
   791	            finally_kind,
   792	        }
   793	    }
   794	
   795	    fn pipeline_assignment(
   796	        &mut self,
   797	        assignment: TypedPipelineAssignment,
   798	    ) -> TypedPipelineAssignment {
   799	        let TypedPipelineAssignment {
   800	            location,
   801	            name,
   802	            value,
   803	        } = assignment;
   804	
   805	        TypedPipelineAssignment {
   806	            location,
   807	            name,
   808	            value: self.boxed_expression(value),
   809	        }
   810	    }
   811	
   812	    fn bit_array(
   813	        &mut self,
   814	        location: SrcSpan,
   815	        type_: Arc<Type>,
   816	        segments: Vec<TypedExprBitArraySegment>,
   817	    ) -> TypedExpr {
   818	        let segments = segments
   819	            .into_iter()
   820	            .map(
   821	                |BitArraySegment {
   822	                     location,
   823	                     value,
   824	                     options,
   825	                     type_,
   826	                 }| BitArraySegment {
   827	                    location,
   828	                    value: self.boxed_expression(value),
   829	                    options: options
   830	                        .into_iter()
   831	                        .map(|bit_array_option| self.bit_array_option(bit_array_option))
   832	                        .collect(),
   833	                    type_,
   834	                },
   835	            )
   836	            .collect();
   837	
   838	        TypedExpr::BitArray {
   839	            location,
   840	            type_,
   841	            segments,
   842	        }

+import gleam/result
+
+pub fn halve_all(a, b, c) {
+  use x <- result.try(divide(a, 2))
+  use y <- result.try(divide(b, 2))
+  use z <- result.map(divide(c, 2))
+
+  #(x, y, z)
+}
+
+fn divide(a, b) {
+  case a % b {
+    0 -> Ok(a / b)
+    _ -> Error(Nil)
+  }
+}
+
+
+----- COMPILED ERLANG
+-module(my@mod).
+-compile([no_auto_import, nowarn_unused_vars, nowarn_unused_function, nowarn_nomatch]).
+-define(FILEPATH, "project/test/my/mod.gleam").
+-export([halve_all/3]).
+
+-file("project/test/my/mod.gleam", 12).
+-spec divide(integer(), integer()) -> {ok, integer()} | {error, nil}.
+divide(A, B) ->
+    case case B of
+        0 -> 0;
+        Gleam@denominator -> A rem Gleam@denominator
+    end of
+        0 ->
+            {ok, case B of
+                    0 -> 0;
+                    Gleam@denominator@1 -> A div Gleam@denominator@1
+                end};
+
+        _ ->
+            {error, nil}
+    end.
+
+-file("project/test/my/mod.gleam", 4).
+-spec halve_all(integer(), integer(), integer()) -> {ok,
+        {integer(), integer(), integer()}} |
+    {error, nil}.
+halve_all(A, B, C) ->
+    case divide(A, 2) of
+        {ok, Value} ->
+            X = Value,
+            case divide(B, 2) of
+                {ok, Value@1} ->
+                    Y = Value@1,
+                    case divide(C, 2) of
+                        {ok, Value@2} ->
+                            {ok, {X, Y, Value@2}};
+
+                        {error, Error} ->
+                            {error, Error}
+                    end;
+
+                {error, Error@1} ->
+                    {error, Error@1}
+            end;
+
+        {error, Error@2} ->
+            {error, Error@2}
+    end.

 /// transform the anonymous function into an intermediate representation.
 struct FindInlinableParameters {
     parameters: HashMap<(EcoString, SrcSpan), bool>,
+    position: FunctionPosition,
+}
+
+#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy)]
+enum FunctionPosition {
+    Body,
+    NestedFunction,
 }
 
 impl FindInlinableParameters {
     fn register_reference(&mut self, name: &EcoString, location: SrcSpan) {
         let key = (name.clone(), location);
+
+        match self.position {
+            FunctionPosition::Body => {}
+            // We don't inline any parameters which are referenced in nested
+            // anonymous function, as our system for inlining parameters cannot
+            // properly handle that case; it requires more complex rewriting of
+            // the code in some cases.
+            FunctionPosition::NestedFunction => {
+                _ = self.parameters.remove(&key);
+                return;
+            }
+        }
+
         match self.parameters.get_mut(&key) {
             Some(true) => _ = self.parameters.remove(&key),
             Some(used @ false) => {
@@ -1025,6 +1031,23 @@ impl<'ast> Visit<'ast> for FindInlinableParameters {
             self.register_reference(name, *location);
         }
     }
+
+    fn visit_typed_expr_fn(
+        &mut self,
+        location: &'ast SrcSpan,
+        type_: &'ast Arc<Type>,
+        kind: &'ast FunctionLiteralKind,
+        args: &'ast [TypedArg],
+        body: &'ast Vec1<TypedStatement>,
+        return_annotation: &'ast Option<ast::TypeAst>,
+    ) {
+        let previous_position = self.position;
+        self.position = FunctionPosition::NestedFunction;
+
+        ast::visit::visit_typed_expr_fn(self, location, type_, kind, args, body, return_annotation);
+
+        self.position = previous_position;
+    }
 }

+import gleam/result
+
+pub fn halve_all(a, b, c) {
+  use x <- result.try(divide(a, 2))
+  use y <- result.try(divide(b, 2))
+  use z <- result.map(divide(c, 2))
+
+  #(x, y, z)
+}
+
+fn divide(a, b) {
+  case a % b {
+    0 -> Ok(a / b)
+    _ -> Error(Nil)
+  }
+}
+
+
+----- COMPILED JAVASCRIPT
+import * as $result from "../../gleam_stdlib/gleam/result.mjs";
+import { Ok, Error, remainderInt, divideInt } from "../gleam.mjs";
+
+function divide(a, b) {
+  let $ = remainderInt(a, b);
+  if ($ === 0) {
+    return new Ok(divideInt(a, b));
+  } else {
+    return new Error(undefined);
+  }
+}
+
+export function halve_all(a, b, c) {
+  let $ = divide(a, 2);
+  if ($ instanceof Ok) {
+    let value = $[0];
+    let x = value;
+    let $1 = divide(b, 2);
+    if ($1 instanceof Ok) {
+      let value$1 = $1[0];
+      let y = value$1;
+      let $2 = divide(c, 2);
+      if ($2 instanceof Ok) {
+        let value$2 = $2[0];
+        return new Ok([x, y, value$2]);
+      } else {
+        let error = $2[0];
+        return new Error(error);
+      }
+    } else {
+      let error = $1[0];
+      return new Error(error);
+    }
+  } else {
+    let error = $[0];
+    return new Error(error);
+  }
+}

   700	    fn inline_anonymous_function_call(
   701	        &mut self,
   702	        parameters: &[TypedArg],
   703	        arguments: Vec<TypedCallArg>,
   704	        body: Vec1<TypedStatement>,
   705	        inlinable_parameters: &[EcoString],
   706	    ) -> TypedExpr {
   707	        // Arguments to this call that can be inlined, and do not need an assignment.
   708	        let mut inline = HashMap::new();
   709	
   710	        // We start by collecting all the assignments for parameters which cannot
   711	        // be inlined.
   712	        let mut statements = parameters
   713	            .iter()
   714	            .zip(arguments)
   715	            .filter_map(|(parameter, argument)| {
   716	                let name = parameter.get_variable_name().cloned().unwrap_or("_".into());
   717	
   718	                // An argument can be inlined if it is only used once (stored in
   719	                // the `InlineFunction` structure), and it is pure. Sometime impure
   720	                // arguments can be inlined, but for simplicity we avoid inlining
   721	                // all impure arguments for now. This heuristic can be improved
   722	                // later.
   723	                if inlinable_parameters.contains(&name)
   724	                    && argument.value.is_pure_value_constructor()
   725	                {
   726	                    _ = inline.insert(name, argument.value);
   727	                    return None;
   728	                }
   729	
   730	                let type_ = argument.value.type_();
   731	
   732	                // Otherwise, we make an assignment which assigns the value of
   733	                // the argument to the correct parameter name.
   734	                Some(Statement::Assignment(Box::new(Assignment {
   735	                    location: BLANK_LOCATION,
   736	                    value: argument.value,
   737	                    pattern: TypedPattern::Variable {
   738	                        location: BLANK_LOCATION,
   739	                        name: name.clone(),
   740	                        type_: type_.clone(),
   741	                        origin: VariableOrigin::generated(),
   742	                    },
   743	                    kind: AssignmentKind::Generated,
   744	                    compiled_case: CompiledCase::simple_variable_assignment(name, type_),
   745	                    annotation: None,
   746	                })))
   747	            })
   748	            .collect_vec();
   749	
   750	        // If we are performing inlining within an already inlined function, there
   751	        // might be inlinable variables in the outer scope. However, these cannot be
   752	        // inlined inside a nested function, so they are saved and restored afterwards.
   753	        let inline_variables = std::mem::replace(&mut self.inline_variables, inline);
   754	
   755	        // Perform inlining on each of the statements in this function's body,
   756	        // potentially inlining parameters and function calls inside this function.
   757	        statements.extend(body.into_iter().map(|statement| self.statement(statement)));
   758	
   759	        self.inline_variables = inline_variables;
   760	
   761	        // We try to expand this block, so a function which is inlined as a
   762	        // single expression does not get wrapped unnecessarily
   763	        expand_block(TypedExpr::Block {
   764	            location: BLANK_LOCATION,
   765	            statements: statements
   766	                .try_into()
   767	                .expect("Type checking ensures there is at least one statement"),
   768	        })

   965

This means that if the same variable is referenced multiple times in the inlined code, only the first occurrence will be replaced, and subsequent occurrences will remain as variables, potentially causing "unbound variable" errors.

When a function is inlined, its parameters that are used multiple times should not be inlined, but the current logic might not properly handle all cases.

   913	fn find_inlinable_parameters(parameters: &[TypedArg], body: &[TypedStatement]) -> Vec<EcoString> {
   914	    let mut parameter_map = HashMap::new();
   915	    for parameter in parameters {
   916	        let (name, location) = match &parameter.names {
   917	            ArgNames::Discard { .. } | ArgNames::LabelledDiscard { .. } => continue,
   918	            ArgNames::Named { name, location }
   919	            | ArgNames::NamedLabelled {
   920	                name,
   921	                name_location: location,
   922	                ..
   923	            } => (name, location),
   924	        };
   925	        _ = parameter_map.insert((name.clone(), *location), false);
   926	    }
   927	
   928	    let mut finder = FindInlinableParameters {
   929	        parameters: parameter_map,
   930	        position: FunctionPosition::Body,
   931	    };
   932	    for statement in body {
   933	        finder.visit_typed_statement(statement);
   934	    }
   935	
   936	    // Inlinable parameters are those that are used exactly once. Any parameters
   937	    // used more than once will be removed from this map and so will not be
   938	    // considered inlinable.
   939	    finder
   940	        .parameters
   941	        .into_iter()
   942	        .filter_map(|((name, _), used)| used.then_some(name))
   943	        .collect()
   944	}

Looking at the `FindInlinableParameters` struct and its `register_reference` method (lines 963-985), I can see the logic:

1. When a parameter is first referenced, it's marked as used (set to `true`)

I need to understand the issue better. The PR description mentions that there's an issue with inlining where a variable `Ssl` is being reported as unbound when it should be resolved. Let me examine the inline logic more carefully.

The problem seems to be in the `FindInlinableParameters` visitor. Looking at the logic:

1. When we encounter a variable reference, if we're in a nested function (`FunctionPosition::NestedFunction`), we remove the parameter from the map
2. However, the logic for handling regular references in `FunctionPosition::Body` only marks it as used once, and if used again, removes it from the map

The issue might be that when we're in a nested function, we're removing parameters even if they haven't been referenced yet, which could cause issues.

2026-01-09 06:17:46,106 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Based on my analysis of the code and the PR description, I've identified the issue with the inlining functionality. The problem is in the `FindInlinableParameters` visitor where parameters are being incorrectly removed from consideration when they're referenced inside nested functions.

Looking at the code in `/testbed/compiler-core/src/inline.rs`, specifically the `register_reference` method in the `FindInlinableParameters` struct (lines 963-985), I found the bug:

## The Issue

When a parameter is referenced inside a nested function, the code removes it from the `parameters` map entirely (line 973: `_ = self.parameters.remove(&key)`). This is incorrect because:

1. The parameter might still be validly used in the outer function scope
2. Removing it from the map prevents it from being considered as an inlinable parameter even if it's only used once in the outer function
3. This can lead to "unbound variable" errors because the parameter is no longer tracked as a local variable

## The Fix

The fix is to only remove parameters from consideration when they're actually referenced multiple times in the outer function scope. When we're in a nested function, we should not modify the outer function's parameter tracking.

Here's the fix:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/compiler-core/src/inline.rs   --old_str '    fn register_reference(&mut self, name: &EcoString, location: SrcSpan) {
        let key = (name.clone(), location);

        match self.position {
            FunctionPosition::Body => {}
            // We don'"'"'t inline any parameters which are referenced in nested
            // anonymous function, as our system for inlining parameters cannot
            // properly handle that case; it requires more complex rewriting of
            // the code in some cases.
            FunctionPosition::NestedFunction => {
                _ = self.parameters.remove(&key);
                return;
            }
        }

        match self.parameters.get_mut(&key) {
            Some(true) => _ = self.parameters.remove(&key),
            Some(used @ false) => {
                *used = true;
            }
            None => {}
        }
    }' --new_str '    fn register_reference(&mut self, name: &EcoString, location: SrcSpan) {
        let key = (name.clone(), location);

        match self.position {
            FunctionPosition::Body => {
                match self.parameters.get_mut(&key) {
                    Some(true) => _ = self.parameters.remove(&key),
                    Some(used @ false) => {
                        *used = true;
                    }
                    None => {}
                }
            }
            // We don'"'"'t inline any parameters which are referenced in nested
            // anonymous function, as our system for inlining parameters cannot
            // properly handle that case; it requires more complex rewriting of
            // the code in some cases.
            FunctionPosition::NestedFunction => {
                // When we'"'"'re in a nested function, we should not modify the outer
                // function'"'"'s parameter tracking. References in nested functions
                // should not affect whether a parameter is inlinable in the outer function.
            }
        }
    }'
